ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reduced-glomerular-filtrate">Reduced glomerular filtrate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reduced-glomerular-filtrate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="occurs-when">Occurs when<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#occurs-when" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Glomerular hydrostatic pressure reduces as in hypotension.</li>
<li>The bowmans space hydrostatic pressure as in ureteric or bladder neck obstruction.</li>
<li>Plasma onchotic pressure increased this occurs in haemaconcentration due to dehydration, multiple myeloma or other dysprotaenaemia.</li>
<li>Renal blood and plasma flow are decreased, this occurs in circulatory collapse.</li>
<li>When there is permeability or total filtering surface area is reduced as it occurs in acute or chronic glomerulonephritis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-kidney">Functions of the kidney<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-kidney" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Responsible for regulation of water thus isoosmotic pressure</li>
<li>Regulation of vasopressin in which help of sodium chloride and urea excretion</li>
<li>Its responsible for regulation of electrolytes</li>
<li>Maintenance of normal base acid balance of body fluids</li>
<li>Retension of vital substances within in the body i.e. proteins</li>
<li>Excretion of metabolic products, toxic substances especially drugs</li>
<li>Responsible for hormonal and metabolic functions i.e. Rennin angiotensin aldosterone and erythropoietin and prostaglandin</li>
</ol>
<p>pg. 4</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-kidney-disease">Signs and symptoms of kidney disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-kidney-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>They are frequently from abnormal in chemical composition of the body or htn, anaemia and metabolic bone disease</p>
<p>Oliguria, polyuria and anuria</p>
<p>Causes of polyuria include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes mellitus</li>
<li>Chronic renal disease due to osmotic and an increase in other areas due to damage of glomerular.</li>
<li>Reduced responsiveness to hormone vasopressin in distal areas commonly in chronic renal disease and recovery phase of acute renal failure</li>
<li>Hypocalcaemia</li>
<li>Hypokalaemia</li>
<li>Inherited nephrogenic diabetes insipidus</li>
<li>Drugs i.e. lasix and those that</li>
<li>Inhibition of vasopressin by drinking a lot of fluids</li>
<li>Psychogenic lesions</li>
</ul>
<p>In case of elimination of edema in congestive cardiac failure or nephrotic syndrome</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations-done-in-the-renal-system">Investigations done in the renal system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations-done-in-the-renal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urinalysis">Urinalysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urinalysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Proteins show glomerular disease i.e. glomerulonephritis, nephrotic syndrome. minimal proteinuria shows pyelonephritis</li>
<li>Glucose shows diabetes mellitus and tubular dysfunction or reabsorption</li>
<li>Ketonuria occurs in metabolic acidosis in condition like starvation and severe ethanol intoxication.</li>
<li>Haematuria myoglobin in haemoglobinuria. the two conditions may cause acute renal failure but in microscopy red blood cells may lack in the urine.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Nitrates, it's formed by conversion of nitrates into nitrite by bacteria in urine. Thus it suggests urinary tract infection or bacteria in the bladder.
&gt; Urine ph, may be between 4.3 _8.0
&gt; Specific gravity is 1.010, low when patients are dehydrated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microscopy">Microscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normal urine has a number of cells and other form of elements which are shed from entire length of urinary tract</p>
<p>An increase in number of cell suggests a disease or formation of new elements</p>
<p>This aids in suggesting site of pathology</p>
<p>Red blood cells one in high-power field normal in men, in female four cell in high power field</p>
<p>An increased red blood cell suggests severe infection, hemorrhagic cystitis and tumor, renal stones and severe inflammation.</p>
<p>Increased white blood cell suggests infection, inflammatory causes and urinary tract infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="casts">Casts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#casts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-renal-failure">Acute renal failure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-renal-failure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Its urine output less than 500mls or complete anuria over 24hrs is significant finding in patients with renal failure.</p>
<ol>
<li>Prerenal</li>
</ol>
<p>This is due to shock as a result</p>
<p> Severe hemorrhage due to arbortion, road RTA, retraplacental haemorrhage, git bleeding.
 Fluid loss as severe burns, diarrhoea and vomiting, dka and Addisons disease, retension of fluid in fistula
 Anesthesia general mostly
 As in cardiac arrest as in cardiac tamponade and pulmonary embolism
 Incompatible blood transfusion
 Allergic reaction</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Renal causes</li>
</ol>
<p>These are renal diseases that lead to renal failure</p>
<p> Acute gloerulonephritis
 Drug poisoning i.e. Sulphonamides and paracetamol.
 Renal artery embolism
 Disseminated intravascular coagulopathy (DIC)
 Infection (there is co direct infection within the renal parenchyma this may cause acute tubular necrosis.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Post renal causes</li>

<p> Bilateral pyelonephritis
 Acute obstructive europathies like</p>
<p> Urethral strictures
 Aneurogenic bladder

 Calculi</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel"></span></span></span></span></span> Urethral congenital valves
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel"></span></span></span></span></span> Primosis</p>
<p>This causes back pressure leading to accumulation of fluid in the renals leading to reduced oxygen perfusion and pressure thus necrosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigation">Investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electrolyte">Electrolyte<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electrolyte" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Maintenance of volume haemastosis and correction of biochemical abnormalities remain the primary goal of treatment and may include the following</p>
<ol>
<li>Correction of fluid overload with furosemide</li>
<li>Correction of severe acidosis with bicarbonate administration, which can be important as abridge of dialysis.</li>
<li>Correction of hyperkalaemia</li>
<li>Correction of hematological</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Correction of fluid overload _furosemide is used in high doses to correct oliguria however response to it indicates a good sign
&gt; Correction of hyperkalamia</p>
<p>In patients with hyperkalaemia its lifethreating.</p>
<p>Approaches in lowering hyperkalaemia include the following</p>
<ul>
<li>Decrease the dietary intake of potassium</li>
<li>Exchanging potassium across gut lumen using potassium binding agents</li>
<li>Promoting intracellular shift in potassium with insulin dextrose solution and beta agonist</li>
<li>Insututing dialysis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nephrotoxic-agents">Nephrotoxic agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nephrotoxic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The kidneys are especially vulnerable to the toxic effects of various chemicals. All nephrotic agents should be avoided or used with extreme caution (NSAIDS)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="vasodilator">Vasodilator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vasodilator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Known to improve renal perfusion thus reducing renal damage.</p>
<p>Dopamine in small doses of 1_5 mcg/kg/min causes selective dilation of the renal vasculature improving perfusion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dietary-modification">Dietary modification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dietary-modification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Dietary changes are an important factor in acute kidney failure</p>
<p>Restriction of salt and fluid becomes a crucial in management of oliguric renal failure.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dialysis</li>
<li>Especially hemodialysis may delay recovery in patients with acute renal failure</li>
<li>Biocompatible membrane hemodialysis is preferred</li>
<li>Indication of dialysis include</li>
<li>Volume expansion that cannot be managed by diuretics</li>
<li>Hyperkalaemia refractory to medical therapy</li>
<li>Correction of severe acid base disturbance that are refractory to medical therapy</li>
<li>Severe azotemia (bun &gt; 80_100)</li>
<li>Uremia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indication-of-dialysis">Indication of dialysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indication-of-dialysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Persistent hyperkalaemia more than 7 mmol/litre</li>
<li>Severe metabolic acidosis less than 7.2 mmol/litre</li>
<li>Refractory pulmonary edema</li>
<li>Uremic pericarditis</li>
<li>Ureamic encephalopathy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complication-of-peritoneal-dialysis">Complication of peritoneal dialysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complication-of-peritoneal-dialysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cardiovascular disease</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Anemia</li>
<li>Renal bone disease</li>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Acquired renal cysts</li>
<li>Malignancy</li>
</ul>
<p>pg. 10</p>
<p>Aluminum injury</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-acute-renal-failure">Complications of acute renal failure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-acute-renal-failure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-renal-failure">CHRONIC RENAL FAILURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-renal-failure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ckd implies long-standing, and usually progressive, impairment in renal function. In many instances, no effective means are available to reverse the primary disease process. Exceptions include correction of urinary tract obstruction, immunosuppressive therapy for systemic vasculitis and good pastures syndrome, treatment of accelerated hypertension, and correction of critical narrowing of renal arteries causing renal impairment.</p>
<p>pg. 11</p>
<p>pg. 12</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="vascular-disease">Vascular disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vascular-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">RISK FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>Obesity Increased Cholesterol</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stages-of-chronic-renal-failure">Stages of chronic renal failure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-chronic-renal-failure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>kidney damage with normal reduced GFR less or equal 90</li>
<li>kidney damage with mild reduced GFR 60_90</li>
<li>moderate reduced GFR 30-59</li>
<li>severe reduced GFR 15-29</li>
<li>kidney failure &lt; 15 (or dialysis)</li>
</ol>
<p>Chronic kidney disease is defined as either kidney damage OR GFR</p>
<p>&lt; 60 ml/min/1.73 m for  3 months</p>
<p>pg. 13</p>
<p>Kidney damage is defined as pathological abnormalities or markers</p>
<p>Of damage, including abnormalities in blood or urine tests or imaging</p>
<p>Studies</p>
<p>From kidney disease outcomes quality initiative of the national</p>
<p>Kidney foundation, USA</p>
<p>Clinical approach to the patient with chronic kidney disease or any other form of renal disease</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history">History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Particular attention should be paid to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Duration of symptoms</li>
<li>Drug ingestion, including non-steroidal anti-inflammatory agents, analgesic and other medications, and unorthodox treatments such as herbal remedies</li>
<li>Previous medical and surgical history, e.g. Previous chemotherapy, multisystem diseases such as SLE, malaria</li>
<li>Previous occasions on which urinalysis or measurement of urea and creatinine might have been performed, e.g. Pre-employment or insurance medical examinations, new patient checks</li>
<li>Family history of renal disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The early stages of renal failure are often completely asymptomatic, despite the accumulation of numerous metabolites.</p>
<p>Serum urea and creatinine concentrations are measured in renal failure since methods for their determination are available</p>
<p>Symptoms are common when the serum urea concentration exceeds 40 mmol/l, but many patients develop uremic symptoms at lower levels of serum urea. Symptoms include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Malaise, loss of energy</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Insomnia</li>
<li>Nocturia and polyuria due to impaired concentrating ability</li>
<li>itching</li>
<li>Nausea, vomiting and diarrhea</li>
<li>Paraesthesia due to polyneuropathy</li>
<li>restless legs syndrome (overwhelming need to frequently alter position of lower limbs)</li>
</ul>
<p>pg. 14</p>
<p>pg. 15</p>
<ul>
<li>Bone pain due to metabolic bone disease</li>
<li>Paraesthesiae and tetany due to hypocalcaemia</li>
<li>Symptoms due to salt and water retention  peripheral or pulmonary edema</li>
<li>Symptoms due to anemia</li>
<li>Amenorrhea in women; erectile dysfunction in men.</li>
</ul>
<p>In more advanced uraemia (serum urea &gt; 5060 mmol/l), these symptoms become more severe, and CNS symptoms are common:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mental slowing, clouding of consciousness, and seizures</li>
<li>Myoclonic twitching.</li>
</ul>
<p>Severe depression of glomerular filtration can result in oliguria.</p>
<p>This can occur with either acute kidney injury or in the terminal stages of chronic kidney disease. However, even if the GFR is profoundly depressed, failure of tubular reabsorption may lead to very high urine volumes; the urine output is therefore not a useful guide to renal function.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination">Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are few physical signs of uraemia per se. Findings include short stature (in patients who have had chronic kidney disease in childhood)</p>
<ul>
<li>Pallor (due to anaemia),</li>
<li>Increased photosensitive pigmentation (which may make the Patient looks misleadingly healthy)</li>
<li>Brown discoloration of the nails</li>
<li>Scratch marks due to uraemic pruritus,</li>
<li>Signs of fluid overload</li>
<li>Pericardial friction rub, flow murmurs (mitral</li>
<li>Regurgitation due to mitral annular calcification, aortic and</li>
<li>Pulmonary regurgitant murmurs due to volume overload),</li>
<li>And glove and stocking peripheral sensory loss (rare).</li>
</ul>
<p>The kidneys themselves are usually impalpable unless grossly enlarged as a result of polycystic disease, obstruction or tumour.</p>
<p>Rectal and vaginal examination may disclose Evidence of an underlying cause of renal failure, particularly Urinary obstruction, and should always be performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-suggestive-of-the-cause">Signs suggestive of the cause<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-suggestive-of-the-cause" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cutaneous vasculitic lesions in systemic vasculitides</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Retinopathy in diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evidence of peripheral vascular disease</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evidence of spina bifida or other causes of neurogenic bladder.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="urinalysis">Urinalysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urinalysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Haematuria may indicate glomerulonephritis, but other sources must be excluded. Haematuria should not be assumed to be due to the presence of an indwelling catheter.</li>
<li>Proteinuria, if heavy, is strongly suggestive of glomerular disease. Urinary infection may also cause proteinuria.</li>
</ul>
<p>Glycosuria with normal blood glucose is common in CKD.</p>
<ul>
<li>Urine culture, including early-morning urine samples for TB.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="urine-microscopy">Urine microscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine-microscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>White cells in the urine usually indicate active bacterial urinary infection, but this is an uncommon cause of renal failure; sterile pyuria suggests papillary necrosis or renal tuberculosis.</li>
<li>Eosinophiluria is strongly suggestive of allergic tubulointerstitial nephritis or cholesterol embolization.</li>
<li>Casts. Granular casts are formed from abnormal cells within the tubular lumen, and indicate active renal disease. Red-cell casts are highly suggestive of glomerulonephritis.</li>
<li>Red cells in the urine may be from anywhere between the glomerulus and the urethral meatus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="urine-biochemistry">Urine biochemistry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine-biochemistry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>24-hour creatinine clearance is sometimes useful in assessing the severity of renal disease.</li>
<li>Measurements of urinary electrolytes are unhelpful in chronic kidney disease. The use of urinary sodium concentration in the distinction between prerenal and intrinsic renal disease</li>
</ul>
<p>pg. 16</p>
<ul>
<li>Urine osmolality is a measure of concentrating ability. A low urine osmolality is normal in the presence of a high fluid intake but indicates renal disease when the kidney should be concentrating urine, such as in hypovolaemia or hypotension.</li>
<li>Urine electrophoresis and immunofixation is necessary for the detection of light chains, which can be present without a detectable serum paraprotein.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="serum-biochemistry">Serum biochemistry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#serum-biochemistry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urea and creatinine with calculation of egger. Electrophoresis and immunofixation for myeloma. Elevations of creatine kinase and a disproportionate elevation in serum creatinine and potassium compared to urea suggest rhabdomyolysis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haematology">Haematology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haematology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Eosinophilia suggests vasculitis, allergic tubulointerstitial nephritis, or cholesterol embolism.</li>
<li>Markedly raised viscosity or ESR suggests myeloma or vasculitis.</li>
<li>Fragmented red cells and/or thrombocytopenia suggest intravascular haemolysis due to accelerated hypertension, hemolytic uraemic syndrome or thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura.</li>
<li>Tests for sickle cell disease should be performed when relevant.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="radiological-investigation">Radiological investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiological-investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ultrasound. Every patient should undergo ultrasonography (for renal size and to exclude hydronephrosis), and plain abdominal radiography and CT (without contrast) to exclude low-density renal stones or nephrocalcinosis, which may be missed on ultrasound.</li>
<li>CT is also useful for the diagnosis of retroperitoneal fibrosis and some other causes of urinary obstruction, and may also demonstrate cortical scarring.</li>
<li>MRI. Magnetic resonance angiography in renovascular disease. For gadolinium used as contrast in renal failure,</li>
<li>Intravenous urography is seldom necessary in advanced renal disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>pg. 17</p>
<p>Management of Chronic Renal Failure</p>
<ul>
<li>Treat underlying cause</li>
<li>Aggressive blood pressure to target values per guidelines sysytolic of 140mm/hg</li>
<li>Management of protein, advice on protein restriction of proteins</li>
<li>Avoid nephrotoxics i.e. NSAIDS</li>
<li>If anemic transfuse or give iron supplements</li>
<li>Incase of hyperphosphotaemia give phosphate binders</li>
<li>Hypocalcaemia replace with calcium supplements i.e. calciterol</li>
<li>Fluid overload give diuretics</li>
<li>Management of hyperlipidaemia to target levels by use of statins</li>
<li>Aggressive glycemic control</li>
<li>Use of ace and arbs in patients with diabetes and proteinuria.</li>
</ul>
<p>COMPLICATIONS OF CHRONIC KIDNEY DISEASE</p>
<p>Anaemia</p>
<p>Bone disease: renal osteodystrophy</p>
<p>The term renal osteodystrophy, more appropriately described as bone mineral disorder, embraces the various forms of bone disease that may develop alone or in combination in chronic kidney disease  hyperparathyroid bone disease, osteomalacia, osteoporosis, osteosclerosis and a dynamic bone disease.</p>
<p>Skin disease</p>
<p>Pruritus (itching) is common in severe renal failure and is usually attributed in the main to retention of nitrogenous waste products of protein catabolism as it improves following the institution of dialysis.</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal complications</p>
<p>pg. 18</p>
<p>These include decreased gastric emptying and increased risk of reflux oesophagitis, peptic ulceration, acute pancreatitis and constipation, particularly in patients on continuous ambulatory peritoneal dialysis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="muscle-dysfunction">Muscle dysfunction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#muscle-dysfunction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Uraemia appears to interfere with muscle energy metabolism, but the mechanism is uncertain. Decreased physical fitness (cardiovascular deconditioning) also contributes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-glomerulonephritis">ACUTE GLOMERULONEPHRITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-glomerulonephritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Its acute inflammation of the glomeruli affecting one or both kidneys</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aetiology">Aetiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Post streptococcal glomerulonephritis</li>
<li>Non strep post infection i.e. bacterial infective endorcaditis, pneumococcal pneumonia, meningocaemia, typhoid fever or syphilis.</li>
<li>Viral infections i.e. hepatitis B, measles, varicela and echovirus</li>
<li>Parasitic infection</li>
<li>Multisystemic disease</li>
<li>Sysytemic lupus erythromatosis</li>
<li>Vasculitis</li>
<li>Good pasture disease</li>
<li>Primary glomerular diseases membrane proliferative glomerulonephritis</li>
<li>Others including</li>
<li>Willims tumor</li>
<li>DPT vaccine</li>
<li>Gullen barree syndrome.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathology">PATHOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is reduction in glomerrular filtration rate thus retention of sodium and water leading to circulatory congestion hypertension and oedema.</p>
<p>pg. 19</p>
<p>Haematuria is due to migration of erythrocytes across the damaged glomerulus and peritubular glomerular cells.</p>
<p>Protenuria is a consequence of loss in anionic changes of capillary wall and selective defect in reabsorb ion</p>
<p>Glomerular filtration rate is reduced due to infiltration of capillaries by inflammatory cells on expansion of number of intrinsic glomerular cells leading to reduced filtration surface area.</p>
<p>Filtration surface area functionally reduced and diffuse endocappilary proliferative glomerulonephritis</p>
<p>There is infiltration of glomerulus with polymorph nuclear cells (monocytes and leukocytes)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It's common in children</p>
<p>It may follow cutenous infections or pharyngeal with group a beta hemolytic streptococcal or history of other infections</p>
<p>Swelling of the face especially in the early mornings</p>
<p>Reduced urine output (coca cola in colour and small in amount)</p>
<p>Painful micturation mixed with blood</p>
<p>Low grade fever</p>
<p>Patients present with symptoms of hypertension.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination-findings">Examination Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Puffy face and ill looking</p>
<p>Edema</p>
<p>Increased bps</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="per-abdomen">Per Abdomen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#per-abdomen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="renal-angle-is-tender">Renal angle is tender<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#renal-angle-is-tender" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigation">Investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urine-for-analysis">Urine for analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine-for-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>May show red blood cells and red blood cast with is an indication of damage to glomerulus</p>
<p>White blood cell casts shows infection or inflammation of the glomerulus</p>
<p>Complete blood count will show reduced haemtocrit demonstrating dilution anemia</p>
<p>pg. 20</p>
<p>Urea, creatinine and electrolyte for estimation of glomerular filtration rate. The BUN and creatinine levels will exhibit levels of renal comprise</p>
<p>ESR is always increased</p>
<p>Imaging test like ultrasonography and CT scan to determine the morphology of the kidneys</p>
<p>Renal biopsy histology determine the therapy and prognosis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bed rest</p>
<p>Monitor vital signs</p>
<p>Urine for albumin levels</p>
<p>Diet and fluid</p>
<ul>
<li>Restrict salt intake</li>
<li>Give fluids where total urine output is more than 500mls</li>
<li>Restrict proteins if urea and keratinize levels are increased</li>
<li>Treat any infection with penicillins</li>
<li>Treat complication of acute glomerulonephritis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-acute-glomerulonephritis">Complications of Acute Glomerulonephritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-acute-glomerulonephritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hypertension</p>
<p>Hypertensive Encephalopathy</p>
<p>Chronic Glomerulonephritis</p>
<p>Uremia</p>
<p>Secondary Infections I.E Bronchitis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-glomerulonephritis">CHRONIC GLOMERULONEPHRITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-glomerulonephritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Its a chronic renal disease resulting to destruction of glomeruli and when fully developed</p>
<p>Causes</p>
<p>AGN in children 50_90 heal completely while the rest 10_50 progress to chronic</p>
<p>pg. 21</p>
<p>Its rapidly becomes proliferative glomerulonephritis</p>
<p>Membrane glomerulonephritis</p>
<p>Others</p>
<ul>
<li>Sysytemic lupus erythromatosis</li>
<li>Henoch schorlenes pupura</li>
<li>Polyarteritis</li>
<li>Good pastures disease</li>
<li>Infective endocarditis</li>
<li>Penicillin poisoning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathology">Pathology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is destruction of the glomerular which may be due to azotemiaor hypertension</p>
<p>Fibrosis of the tubules, glomeruli reduced and nephrosclerosis</p>
<p>Chronic glomerulonephritis invariably leads to chronic renal failure once these happens it causes abnormalities in the body due to</p>
<ul>
<li>Nephrons insensitivity to aldosterone</li>
<li>Electrolyte imbalance</li>
<li>Acid _base imbalance</li>
<li>Uremia</li>
</ul>
<p>Clinical features</p>
<ul>
<li>Due to uremia and hypertension</li>
<li>Patient may have no signs and symptoms</li>
<li>Routine blood pressure shows hypertension</li>
<li>Patients may have anemia, normacytic normochromic</li>
<li>Present history of AGN</li>
<li>Obvious features of chronic renal failure which include</li>
<li>Yellow ness of the eyes accompanied with anemia</li>
<li>CVS, hypertension, left ventricular hypertrophy, Cardiac arrest due to increased potassium, pericarditis secondary to uremia</li>
<li>R/S features of acidosis evident with kusmall breathing.</li>
<li>GUT poluria and polydypsia</li>
</ul>
<p>pg. 22</p>
<p>GIT nausea, vomiting, malena stool, epigastric pains, hematemesis, ulceration of the mouth, bitter saliva</p>
<p>CNS fits, tremors, drawiness, coma.</p>
<p>Hematological system; anemia due to uremia which causes depression of the bone marrow, heamolysis and may lead to bleeding tendencies</p>
<p>Erythropoietin due to depression of the parenchyma cells.</p>
<p>Investigation</p>
<p>a) Urine for specific gravity, proteins, RBC casts, culture and sensitivity, hyaline cast is typical of CGN
b) Serum for urea levels, potassium levels, creatinine levels and phosphate, calcium and sodium levels
c) Full haemogram shows evidence of anaemia iron deficiency
d) Bone xray to check for features of oestomalasia and oestiofibrosa or osteoporosis
e) CHEST XRAY to rule out left ventricular failure and cardiac failure.
f) Intravenous urography to rule out any obstruction to urine out flow and size of the kidney
g) Ultrasonography to check for the size of the kidneys and any calcifications and urine stones.</p>
<p>Treatment</p>
<p>Give low protein diet around 20_40 g/day</p>
<p>Give IV fluids n/s 2_5 litres alternating with dextrose</p>
<p>If there is hypertension and oedema salt is restricted</p>
<p>Renal disease thiazides are avoided</p>
<p>If there is infection antibiotics are given</p>
<p>Hypertensive gives ACE</p>
<p>Bone pains give calciferol 5mg bd</p>
<p>If anaemic give iron supplements</p>
<p>If no improvement dialysis is preferred.</p>
<p>pg. 23</p>
<p>pg. 24</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nephrotic-syndrome">NEPHROTIC SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nephrotic-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Its arenal disease characterised by</p>
<ul>
<li>Protenuria or albinuria</li>
<li>Hyponatremia</li>
<li>Massive edema</li>
<li>Hypercholestremia</li>
</ul>
<p>It happen due to increased permeability of the glomerulus</p>
<p>It's divided into</p>
<p> Primary nephritoc syndrome</p>
<ul>
<li>Focal or segmental glomerulonephritis</li>
<li>Minimum change glomerulonephritis</li>
<li>Membrane proliferative glomerulonephritis</li>
</ul>
<p> Secondary type</p>
<p>Its associated with</p>
<ul>
<li>Infections parasitic i.e malaria and schistossomia, bacterial i.e post strep glomerulonephritis</li>
<li>Drugs i.e mercury, penicillins and gold</li>
<li>Hereditary causes i.e diabetes, congenital nephrotic syndrome</li>
<li>Malignancies I.e Hodgkin's disease, leukemia and willies disease</li>
<li>Connective tissue disease</li>
<li>Systemic lupus erythromatosis</li>
<li>Good pasture disease its alung disease that someone coughs blood is anaemic and may have kidney disease.</li>
<li>Syogens disease</li>
<li>Amyloidosis and sarcoidosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathogenesis">Pathogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Increased permeability of glomerulus causes leakage of proteins in urine 3.5m/24hrs</p>
<p>Hyponatremia leading to reduction in onchotic pressure thus fluid enter intercellular spaces this reduces effective plasma cells and leads to passive edema</p>
<p>Reduction in plasma volume stimulates rennin_ angiotensin aldosterone system leading to retention of sodium increasing thus edema.</p>
<p>ADH system is also stimulated leading to more fluid retention.</p>
<p>The sympathetic system is also stimulated leading to more fluid retention.</p>
<p>Increased loss of lipoproteins which are responsible for transporting lipids leads to hypercholesterol in blood</p>
<p>Due to loss of iodine bound albumin this may lead to hypothyroidism a negative feedback thus increased production of thyroid hormone leading to goiter.</p>
<p>Due to loss of transferring proteins responsible for transfer of iron leads to iron resistance anaemia. blood picture is microcytic hyochromic type of anemia.</p>
<p>There will be hypocalcaemia due to lack of vitamin D</p>
<p>Loss of thrombin 111 also called Heparin CO factor leading to increased coagulibility thus microembolism and thromboembolism.</p>
<p>Most patients present with pain in loins and haematuria due to bilateral renal thrombosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigation">Investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
